### Fixed
- fix(release): vBRIEF-lifecycle-sync gate now scales by vBRIEF-referenced-issue-count, not repo-open-issue-count -- inverted lookup via batched gh api graphql retires the 200-issue pagination cap and the Tier 2 truncation-guard surface (#754)
- **fix(scripts/release_e2e.py): pass `--allow-vbrief-drift` to dispatched `task release` against the auto-created temp repo** (post-#754 harness fix, refs #720 e2e harness, refs #734 lifecycle gate). The temp rehearsal repo is created empty (zero issues), so the inverted-lookup vBRIEF-lifecycle-sync gate from #754 classifies every referenced issue number as NOT_FOUND -> Section (c) mismatch and the inner pipeline fails at Step 3. The escape hatch is the correct surface to bypass the gate in the rehearsal context; the production cut path against a real repo does NOT pass this flag and remains fully gated. Latent since #734 landed (April 29) -- the v0.21.0 cut session never ran `task release:e2e` post-#734, so the regression surfaced today during the v0.22.0 Phase 3 e2e gate. `tests/cli/test_release_e2e.py::TestDispatchTaskRelease::test_argv_carries_allow_vbrief_drift` regression-guards the flag.
- **fix(.github/workflows/release.yml): release job no longer auto-flips draft -> public** (#733, refs #716): The workflow's `release` job ran `softprops/action-gh-release@v2` without `draft: true`, and the action defaults `draft` to `false` -- so every tag push silently flipped the GitHub release from draft (created locally by `task release`) to public, bypassing the #716 Phase 5 user-only authority gate. Fix sets `draft: true` explicitly on the softprops step so the workflow becomes BUILD AND UPLOAD only and `task release:publish` remains the sole authorised path that flips draft -> public. New `tests/content/test_release_workflow.py` parses `.github/workflows/release.yml` and asserts no softprops usage with `draft: false` or unset, no `gh release edit --draft=false` step, and no other isDraft-flipping pattern (defensive regex scan for `"draft": false` JSON bodies and `is_draft: false` aliases). Also adds a new `verify-run-version` job in the same workflow per #741 (separate `### Fixed` entry below) that fails the release on a tag push when `run`'s resolved VERSION disagrees with the pushed tag, closing the regression loop for future drift.
- **fix(run, .github/workflows/release.yml): dynamic VERSION resolution in `run`; CI assertion against pushed tag** (#741, refs #723 sibling Taskfile-side dynamic resolver, refs #74 / #716 release foundation): The hard-coded `VERSION = "X.Y.Z"` literal in `run` was the root cause of the v0.21.0 stale-version incident -- nothing in the release pipeline updated the literal, so `run --help` reported `0.20.0` for weeks after the v0.21.0 tag landed. Path A (locked per swarm-prep) removes the literal entirely. The replacement is an inline priority chain mirroring `scripts/resolve_version.py::resolve_version()`: (1) `$DEFT_RELEASE_VERSION` env override (set by `scripts/release.py::run_build` so `task release -- 0.X.Y` pins the in-flight version); (2) `git describe --tags --abbrev=0` with leading `v` stripped (ordinary tagged checkouts); (3) `0.0.0-dev` fallback for fresh checkouts with no tags or repositories where `git` is unavailable. The chain is intentionally inlined rather than imported from `scripts/resolve_version.py` because `run` is the framework's bootstrap entry point -- the two implementations are kept in lockstep by convention and pinned by parallel regression coverage. `.github/workflows/release.yml` gains a `verify-run-version` job that fetches full tag history, imports `run` to resolve VERSION via the priority chain, and fails the workflow on tag push if the resolved value disagrees with `${GITHUB_REF_NAME#v}` -- defence against future drift regardless of which fix path was taken. New `tests/cli/test_run_version.py` (14 tests across `TestPriorityChain`, `TestNoLiteralVersion`, and a smoke test) cover env override / git tag stripping / dev fallback / priority order / whitespace handling AND a forbid-the-literal guard scan of `run` source so the regression cannot recur. Tests live in a sibling module rather than extending `tests/cli/test_release.py` because that file is already 1771 lines (over the AGENTS.md 1000-line MUST limit), mirroring the established `test_release_skip_flags.py` / `test_release_summary.py` split-out pattern.

### Removed

## [0.21.0] - 2026-04-29

> First deft version with deterministic release tooling — `task release` (#74) and `task ci:local` (#233) — plus the [AXIOM] rule hierarchy (#642), Rule Ownership Map enforcement (#635), and codified orchestrator role-separation (#727). Self-validated: the cycle exercised the rollback safety net AND deepened e2e harness end-to-end, surfacing 6 pipeline defects (5 in the rollback cycle + #731 in the e2e gate this cut), all fixed before re-cut.

### Added
- **feat(scripts,skills): release CHANGELOG promotion accepts `--summary` blockquote** (release-narrative-gap, refs #74 release pipeline parent, refs #716 Phase 8 Slack template surface, refs #727 orchestrator role-separation): Closes the gap surfaced during v0.21.0 re-cut prep where the post-publish narrative was hand-authored three times (CHANGELOG `[<version>]` section, GitHub release body, Slack `*Summary*:` slot) and drifted across audiences. New optional `--summary TEXT` flag on `scripts/release.py` (and `task release -- <version> --summary "<text>"`) injects a one-line Markdown blockquote (`> <summary>`) directly after the promoted `## [<version>] - <date>` heading, sandwiched by blank lines for proper Keep-a-Changelog rendering. Backward-compatible: `summary=None` (or empty / omitted) preserves pre-existing behaviour byte-for-byte. The blockquote is inline Markdown (operators may include `**bold**`, `[link](url)`, etc. -- preserved verbatim, no escaping); embedded newlines raise `ValueError` (single-line slot). The same blockquote naturally flows into the GitHub release body via the existing `_section_for_version` pickup AND is the canonical source for the Phase 8 Slack `*Summary*:` slot per `skills/deft-directive-release/SKILL.md`. (Tier 1 primary) `scripts/release.py::promote_changelog(text, version, repo, today, summary=None)` extends the existing pure function; `ReleaseConfig` gains `summary: str | None = None`; `_build_parser` adds `--summary TEXT` (helptext cites 80-160 char recommendation + the three-surface flow); `run_pipeline` Step 4 threads `summary=config.summary` through and the dry-run preview reflects whether a summary was supplied (truncated to ~60 chars) so operators can validate the wording during Phase 2 before any file is written; `main` wires `args.summary` to `ReleaseConfig.summary`. (Tier 4 secondary) `skills/deft-directive-release/SKILL.md` Phase 1 gains a `~` step asking the operator for the optional one-line summary (recommended 80-160 chars; can be skipped) and a ⊗ anti-pattern against per-audience hand-writing; Phase 2 dry-run command demonstrates `--summary` pass-through; Phase 4 production draft passes `--summary`; Phase 8 Slack `*Summary*:` populate rule documents verbatim copy from the CHANGELOG blockquote with a fallback for skipped Phase 1; new ⊗ anti-pattern in the Anti-Patterns block prohibits manually rewriting the Slack summary to deviate from CHANGELOG (creates documentation drift). (Tier 5 tertiary) `scm/changelog.md` gains an `## Optional Release Summary Blockquote` section documenting the structural shape and the `--summary` provenance, with a ⊗ anti-pattern mirroring the SKILL one. New tests in `tests/cli/test_release_summary.py` (split from `test_release.py` to keep that file under the 1000-line MUST limit per AGENTS.md, mirroring the `test_release_skip_flags.py` pattern from #720) cover: `test_promote_changelog_with_summary` (`\n\n> Test summary\n` between heading and `### Added`); `test_promote_changelog_without_summary` (backward-compat regression guard); `test_promote_changelog_summary_with_markdown` (inline Markdown preserved verbatim); `test_promote_changelog_summary_empty_string` (`summary=""` byte-identical to `summary=None`); `test_promote_changelog_summary_with_newline` (`\n` and `\r` raise `ValueError`); `test_main_summary_argparse` (`--summary` lands in `ReleaseConfig.summary`); `test_pipeline_summary_threaded` (Step 4 dry-run preview surfaces the wording for operator validation). Scope vBRIEF: `vbrief/proposed/2026-04-29-release-summary-blockquote.vbrief.json`.

- **feat(scripts,tasks,skills,docs): release safety hardening (#716, refs #74 foundation, refs #233 More Determinism umbrella, refs #642 workflow umbrella, refs #635 epic anchor, refs #709 Repair Authority [AXIOM] -- this PR demonstrates the rule by landing the safety net atomically with the foundation rather than deferring to a follow-up, refs #710 data-file-conventions follow-up, refs #633 pre-PR deterministic CI enforcement umbrella)**: Expands the `task release` foundation (Item below) with the full safety net per the canonical [#716 spec](https://github.com/deftai/directive/issues/716), so master never enters a "release-without-rollback" state. Seven coordinated artifacts: (1) `scripts/release.py` defaults `gh release create` to `--draft` and exposes `--no-draft` for the rare direct-publish case (e.g. automated security patches); the Step-10 pipeline label suffixes `(draft)` / `(PUBLIC)` and the dry-run preview surfaces `--draft` in the operator-readable plan -- this decouples the *artifact production* phase (release.yml CI + binary upload) from the *consumer-visibility* phase. (2) `scripts/release_publish.py` + `task release:publish -- <version>` flips a draft to public via `gh release edit --draft=false`; four-state machine (`draft` -> proceed; already-`published` -> exit 0 no-op; `not-found` -> exit 1; `gh-error` -> exit 1) with a post-edit re-read verifying `isDraft` actually flipped (catches stale-cache / silent-noop / wrong-tag cases). (3) `scripts/release_rollback.py` + `task release:rollback -- <version>` performs a state-aware unwind across four detected states (local commit + tag, tag pushed no release, release published with downloads <= guard, release published with downloads > guard) with a **time-windowed download-count guard** per #716 Q3 (release age < 5 min -> threshold = 0; 5-30 min -> threshold = max(--allow-low-downloads, 10) to filter bot fetches; > 30 min -> refuse without --allow-data-loss because downloads are likely consumer-driven), three escape hatches (`--allow-low-downloads N`, `--allow-data-loss`, `--force-strict-0` for security-incident hot-rollbacks), and a **race-condition double-read** of `download_count` (read, sleep 5s, re-read; only proceed if both reads agree below threshold -- catches a real consumer download arriving between the probe and the unwind, since GitHub's release-asset cache has ~30s staleness). (4) `scripts/release_e2e.py` + `task release:e2e` rehearses the full pipeline against an **auto-created + auto-destroyed temp GitHub repo** per #716 Q1 (`gh repo create --private deftai/deftai-release-test-<timestamp>-<uuid6>` -> rehearsal -> `gh repo delete --yes` in a `try/finally` clause so cleanup ALWAYS runs, even when the rehearsal failed; cleanup-failure surfaces a one-line manual-cleanup hint as a WARN and preserves the rehearsal exit code -- operator never sees "rehearsal succeeded" reported as "cleanup failed"); `--keep-repo` skips destroy for manual debugging; `--dry-run` invokes no gh helpers. (5) `skills/deft-directive-release/SKILL.md` + `.agents/skills/deft-directive-release/SKILL.md` thin pointer carry the **8-phase workflow** that operationalizes the entire surface: Phase 1 pre-flight (base branch, clean tree, version-bump magnitude vs CHANGELOG content, `task ci:local`, `gh auth status`); Phase 2 dry-run review with user-gate `yes`/`back`/`quit` mirroring `deft-directive-review-cycle`; Phase 3 e2e sanity against a temp repo; Phase 4 production draft via `task release -- <ver>`; Phase 5 user-only-authority draft review gate (`publish` / `rollback` / `defer`); Phase 6 branches on the user choice; Phase 7 post-publish verification (closing-keyword Layer 1 + Layer 3 reopen sweep, binary download check, ROADMAP correctness); Phase 8 generates the Slack release announcement re-using the canonical block from `skills/deft-directive-swarm/SKILL.md` Phase 6 Step 5 (single source of truth). (6) `AGENTS.md` skill-routing entry maps `"release"` / `"cut release"` / `"v0.X.Y"` / `"publish release"` -> `skills/deft-directive-release/SKILL.md` and cross-references the swarm Slack-announcement template. (7) Three-state exit codes (`0` success, `1` violation/refusal, `2` config error) match the conventions of `scripts/release.py`, `scripts/pr_check_protected_issues.py` (#702), and `scripts/rule_ownership_lint.py` (#705). Tests: 96 new tests across `tests/cli/test_release.py` (8 new for default-draft), `tests/cli/test_release_publish.py` (19), `tests/cli/test_release_rollback.py` (51), `tests/cli/test_release_e2e.py` (18) -- all use mocks on subprocess / gh / git helpers so CI never hits real GitHub. Encoding-safety pattern preserved: every file edit goes through Python `pathlib.Path.write_text(text, encoding="utf-8")`; PowerShell file edits use `--body-file` redirection for non-ASCII content. Closes #716. The companion `task release` foundation (Item below) closes #74; both discrete-task issues land in the same atomic PR per Repair Authority [AXIOM] (#709) so master is never in a release-without-rollback state.
- **feat(scripts,tasks,tests): `task release` automation -- changelog promote, roadmap move, tag, gh release** (#74, refs #233 More Determinism umbrella, refs #642 workflow umbrella, refs #635 epic anchor, refs #709 Repair Authority [AXIOM], refs #710 data-file-conventions check follow-up): Lands the deterministic encoding of the v0.X.Y release flow per #74. Three coordinated artifacts: (1) `scripts/release.py` -- argparse + pathlib + subprocess pipeline (`pre-flight git status` -> `pre-flight branch == master` -> `pre-flight CI` -> `CHANGELOG promotion` -> `ROADMAP refresh` -> `task build` -> `git tag -a vX.Y.Z` -> `git push origin vX.Y.Z` -> `gh release create vX.Y.Z`) with three-state exit codes (0 success / 1 violation / 2 config error) following the conventions of `scripts/pr_check_protected_issues.py` (#702) and `scripts/rule_ownership_lint.py` (#705). The `--dry-run` flag prints the full plan without writing files or invoking external commands; `--skip-tag` suppresses both `git tag` and `git push origin <tag>`; `--skip-release` suppresses `gh release create`; `--allow-dirty` bypasses the dirty-tree pre-flight (rehearsals only); `--repo OWNER/REPO` overrides the default resolution chain (`--repo` flag > `git remote get-url origin` parse > `deftai/directive` constant fallback). The CI step prefers `task ci:local` when present and falls back gracefully to `task check` when not -- the fallback exists because `task ci:local` is the sibling work item under the same #233 umbrella (in flight as agent2 in this swarm); both targets are detected via `task --list-all` regex match. CHANGELOG promotion is the single-source-of-truth pure function `promote_changelog(text, version, repo, today)`: locates the `## [Unreleased]` heading, renames it to `## [<version>] - <YYYY-MM-DD>`, inserts a fresh empty `## [Unreleased]` block (with the four canonical sub-sections) immediately above, rewrites the trailing `[Unreleased]:` link footer to `compare/v<version>...HEAD`, and appends a new `[<version>]: compare/v<previous>...v<version>` entry mirroring the existing footnote pattern (greenfield `releases/tag/v<version>` fallback when no previous version exists). ROADMAP move-to-completed delegates to the existing `task roadmap:render` (idempotent renderer aggregating `vbrief/pending/` Active + `vbrief/completed/` Completed) so vBRIEFs that should appear in `## Completed` are expected to have been moved via `task scope:complete` in advance -- the release script trusts the renderer rather than mutating ROADMAP.md directly. (2) `tasks/release.yml` -- new sub-Taskfile wrapping `uv run python {{.DEFT_ROOT}}/scripts/release.py {{.CLI_ARGS}}` with `dir: '{{.USER_WORKING_DIR}}'` (consumer-safe per #535) and `env: PYTHONUTF8: "1"` (#540 belt-and-suspenders); intentionally NO `sources:` / `generates:` per `conventions/task-caching.md` (#574) since `--dry-run` / `--skip-tag` / `--skip-release` / `--allow-dirty` / `--repo` are user-facing recovery flags that MUST NOT be silently dropped by go-task's incremental-build cache. The `release: ./tasks/release.yml` include is added to the root `Taskfile.yml` alongside the existing entries. (3) `tests/cli/test_release.py` -- 30+ tests using the in-process `importlib.util.spec_from_file_location` pattern from `tests/cli/test_pr_check_protected_issues.py` and `tests/cli/test_rule_ownership_lint.py`, covering `_validate_version` (parametrized valid + invalid), `_resolve_repo` (flag / https / ssh / failure / unparseable / git-missing), `promote_changelog` (heading rename, fresh Unreleased block, sub-sections preserved, compare link, Unreleased compare update, order preserved, greenfield, missing-Unreleased ValueError, idempotent), `_section_for_version`, `_split_body_and_links`, `task_has_target`, `run_ci` (prefers ci:local, falls back to check, neither, non-zero exit -- proves the **CI fallback** while `task ci:local` is in-flight), pipeline (dry-run no-writes, dirty-tree refused without `--allow-dirty` exit 1, dirty-tree accepted with the flag, wrong branch refused exit 1, `--skip-tag` suppresses git, `--skip-release` suppresses gh, CI failure exit 1, CHANGELOG missing exit 2, CHANGELOG-without-Unreleased exit 2), `main` (invalid version exit 2, missing positional argparse exit 2, `--help` exit 0, dry-run round-trip byte-identical), and a subprocess smoke test for `--help`. PowerShell encoding-safety pattern: every file edit goes through Python `pathlib.Path.write_text(text, encoding="utf-8")` -- no inline PS string ops on text containing non-ASCII. Closes #74. The pipeline now stages and commits CHANGELOG.md / ROADMAP.md (via `commit_release_artifacts`) BEFORE invoking `git tag -a vX.Y.Z`, then uses `git push --atomic origin <base-branch> vX.Y.Z` so the annotated tag and resulting GitHub release always anchor to the promoted commit and the working tree is clean post-pipeline (Greptile P1 review on PR #712 surfaced the missing-commit gap; the previous code would have tagged the pre-release HEAD and left a dirty tree).
- **feat(scripts,tasks,tests): `task ci:local` -- run the full CI pipeline locally (matrix-aware)** (#233 plan.item `task-ci-local`, refs #642 workflow umbrella, refs #635 epic anchor, refs #74 sibling sub-agent A `task release` PR, refs #709 Repair Authority [AXIOM], refs #633 pre-PR deterministic-CI enforcement umbrella, refs #710 data-file-conventions check follow-up): New `task ci:local` (Taskfile target in `tasks/ci.yml`, dispatches `uv run python {{.DEFT_ROOT}}/scripts/ci_local.py`) replicates the step graph of `.github/workflows/ci.yml` on the host platform so contributors catch CI failures before pushing -- mirrors the `python` job (uv sync + ruff + mypy tests/ + pytest --cov), the `go` job (go test ./cmd/deft-install/ + cross-compile builds for linux/amd64, darwin/arm64, windows/amd64), and the existing Taskfile-level verifications (`toolchain:check`, `verify:stubs`, `verify:links`, `verify:rule-ownership`, `vbrief:validate`, `build`); the Windows-only `windows-task-dispatch` regression pytest guard-rails are gated behind `--matrix=windows` AND a Windows host. New `scripts/ci_local.py` follows the argparse + pathlib + subprocess pattern of `scripts/rule_ownership_lint.py` (#705) and `scripts/pr_check_protected_issues.py` (#702): three-state exit codes (0 = every applicable step succeeded; 1 = at least one step failed; 2 = configuration error -- no applicable steps, missing root); flags `--matrix=<linux|macos|windows|all|host>` (default: host), `--skip-build` (skip cross-compile + `task build` + `task build:verify` for tight inner-loop iteration), `--verbose` (mirror CI logs verbatim, stream every step's stdout/stderr even on success), `--fail-fast` / `--no-fail-fast` (default fail-fast aborts the pipeline on the first failure; `--no-fail-fast` runs every applicable step and still reports a non-zero exit when any failed); per-step output of the form `[N/M] <step name>... OK (X.XXs)` / `FAIL` mirrors the GitHub Actions log style for debugging parity, with full stdout/stderr capture surfaced on failure (or always under `--verbose`); a final aggregate report prints total / passed / failed / skipped counts plus elapsed time and per-step diagnostics. The `task build:verify` step is detected at runtime via `task --list` and skipped with an informational message (not a failure) when missing -- it's a sibling pending #233 plan.item; once it lands the same `ci:local` invocation picks it up automatically. Per `conventions/task-caching.md` the new task forwards `{{.CLI_ARGS}}` to the script and intentionally declares no `sources:` / `generates:` so flags like `--skip-build` / `--no-fail-fast` are never silently swallowed by go-task's incremental-build cache. `Taskfile.yml` includes block gains a new `ci: ./tasks/ci.yml` (optional) entry, appended after `pr:` to keep the merge-cascade rebase against sibling sub-agent A's `release:` include addition mechanical (append-only ordering). Inline platform differences are documented in both `scripts/ci_local.py`'s module docstring and `tasks/ci.yml`'s top-of-file comment block: Linux/macOS use `/dev/null` as the cross-compile discard target; Windows uses `NUL`; Windows-task-dispatch regressions only run on a real Windows host because the steps shell out to PowerShell; per the existing PowerShell 5.1 encoding-safety pattern, the script writes nothing inline that requires non-ASCII string ops -- the on-disk artifacts (PR bodies, status files) are produced via `pathlib` / `create_file` and consumed via `--body-file` so multi-byte UTF-8 characters never round-trip through PowerShell's UTF-16LE internals. New `tests/cli/test_ci_local.py` (48 tests) loads `scripts/ci_local.py` in-process via `importlib.util` (registers the module in `sys.modules` before `exec_module` so the stdlib `@dataclass` introspection helpers can resolve `cls.__module__`) and covers: argument parsing for every flag including the mutually-exclusive `--fail-fast` / `--no-fail-fast` pair; host-matrix mapping (Linux/Darwin/Windows hosts plus the FreeBSD fallback); pipeline composition under each matrix and `--skip-build`; the `task build:verify` graceful-absence + present branches; the `windows-task-dispatch` row's gating on host AND matrix; runner OK/FAIL/SKIP behaviour including verbose stdout/stderr mirroring on success and the `--- stdout --- / --- stderr ---` diagnostic block on failure; fail-fast aborts subsequent steps with `aborted -- earlier step failed and --fail-fast is set` reasons; `--no-fail-fast` lets every step run; the `FileNotFoundError` path on a missing executable is surfaced as a fail row; aggregate-report counts and elapsed-time formatting; `main()` exit-code triplet (0 OK / 1 step failure / 2 config error); a synthetic round-trip that asserts the runner walks the expected step order and that the aggregate summary lands on stdout. Per acceptance criteria the umbrella issue #233 stays OPEN as the GitHub-side tracker for the 5 remaining pending items in the More Determinism vBRIEF (`vbrief/pending/2026-04-23-233-more-determinism-full-initiative-phase-0-spec.vbrief.json` -- Phase 0 generated per-phase gates, task doctor, build:verify, change:archive, task release); only the `task-ci-local` plan.item resolves with this PR.

Exit codes: 0 = clean; 1 = drift detected (rule moved, section renamed, text rewritten -- diagnostic identifies which row, which file, and what was looked for); 2 = config error (data file missing, malformed JSON, schema violation, duplicate id, unknown authority). - **feat(events): wire 5 detection-bound events under epic #635** (#635, refs #642): Lands the structural events surface for the 5 detection-bound framework events whose detectors already exist (`pre-cutover:detected`, `vbrief:invalid`, `agents-md:stale`, `version:drift`, `dirty-tree:detected`) per the canonical [#642 workflow comment](https://github.com/deftai/directive/issues/642#issuecomment-4330742436). New `events/registry.json` (data file) plus `events/registry.schema.json` and `events/event-record.schema.json` document each event's payload contract, detector pointer, and consumer pointers. New `scripts/_event_detect.py::emit(name, payload)` builds a uniform `{event, detected_at, payload}` record, validates the name against the registry (raises `EventEmissionError` on typos), caps payload list values at 50 entries, and optionally appends each emission to a `DEFT_EVENT_LOG` JSON-lines file (silent by default). New `scripts/_event_detect.py::detect_agents_md_stale(project_root)` codifies the QUICK-START.md Step 2b detection logic (parses AGENTS.md for `deft/skills/<name>/SKILL.md` tokens, checks each path's existence and the first 200 chars for the `<!-- deft:deprecated-skill-redirect -->` sentinel) so the AGENTS.md-stale event has a Python detection point alongside the prose-encoded version. Wired emit call sites: `scripts/vbrief_validate.py::validate_all` emits `vbrief:invalid` whenever errors or warnings surface; `scripts/migrate_vbrief.py::migrate` emits `dirty-tree:detected` when the dirty-tree guard trips; `run::_check_upgrade_gate` emits `version:drift` on `.deft-version` mismatch and `pre-cutover:detected` when SPECIFICATION.md / PROJECT.md lack the redirect sentinel; `run::_check_upgrade_gate` also runs `detect_agents_md_stale` and emits `agents-md:stale` when stale skill paths surface. All emit calls swallow registry/IO errors so existing CLI behavior (exit codes, stdout/stderr text, refusal messages) is preserved verbatim. `tasks/migrate.yml` `migrate:vbrief` description references the emitted events for discoverability. Filename note: the helper is `scripts/_event_detect.py` (not `scripts/_events.py`) to avoid file-level merge conflict with the sibling events-behavioral vBRIEF; post-merge consolidation may unify them under one canonical name. New `tests/cli/test_events.py` (17 tests) covers registry shape, schema self-description, the 5 expected event names + categories, emit() record shape against `event-record.schema.json`, unregistered-name rejection, `DEFT_EVENT_LOG` append behavior, payload list truncation, `detect_agents_md_stale` against missing/redirect/clean fixtures + de-duplication, and end-to-end emit wiring for `vbrief:invalid` and `dirty-tree:detected`.
- **Rule Authority [AXIOM]** in `main.md`: peer `## Rule Authority [AXIOM]` section after Persona encoding the V4 hierarchy (deterministic > Taskfile > vBRIEF > RFC2119 > prose); prose is fallback only. Cross-references #634 (detection-tier ladder) and #642 (umbrella). (#642, PR #401)
- **Codebase hygiene rules** in `coding/hygiene.md` plus consistent Hygiene sections across 11 mainstream language files (`languages/*.md`); promotes ongoing health (dead code, circular deps, error hiding, legacy, DRY, comments) to a first-class concern. (#642, PR #401)
- **docs(meta/lessons): codify GitHub closing-keyword false-positive lesson**: Appended a new `## GitHub Closing-Keyword False-Positive in Negation Context (2026-04)` section to `meta/lessons.md` capturing the #697 incident where issue #642 was auto-closed on squash merge despite the PR body intentionally avoiding `Closes`. Root cause: GitHub's closing-keyword parser is substring-based and matches `Closes #N` / `Fixes #N` / `Resolves #N` regardless of surrounding context (including negation parentheticals like "Intentionally not `Closes #642`"). Lesson includes (1) MUST NOT rule against writing closing keywords in negation/quotation/example contexts in PR bodies, (2) recommended alternative phrasings ("Intentionally NOT using a closing keyword for #N", `Refs #N (tracking umbrella; remains open)`), and (3) reinforcement that post-merge issue-state verification (#167's existing rule) catches both failure directions -- not just "should have closed but didn't" but also "should have stayed open but was auto-closed". Cross-references existing PR Merge Hygiene lesson #1 (#167), `scm/github.md`, and `skills/deft-directive-review-cycle/SKILL.md` Post-Merge Verification.
- **docs(skills,meta/lessons,tasks): codify Layer 3 closing-keyword false-positive (persistent GitHub-side `closingIssuesReferences` link)** (#701, refs #575, #633): Hardens the swarm/merge workflow against the third layer of the closing-keyword false-positive surfaced by workflow #642 -- two real incidents where umbrella issues auto-closed on squash merge despite the PR body being amended to `Refs #N` only (no closing keywords in the PR body, in commit messages, or in the explicit `--subject` / `--body-file` squash payload): PR #700 closed #233 (concatenated commit-message variant) and PR #401 closed #642 (persistent-link variant). Root cause: GitHub's `closingIssuesReferences` link is durable -- recorded the moment a closing keyword first appears in a PR body or an issue is attached via the Development sidebar, and survives every subsequent body / commit-message / squash-payload edit. **Primary encoding** lives in `skills/deft-directive-swarm/SKILL.md` Phase 6 Step 1 (per the Rule Authority [AXIOM] block in `main.md`, skill = RFC2119 with structured triggers is a stronger encoding than prose): added (1) a `!` (MUST) pre-merge `gh pr view <N> --json closingIssuesReferences` inspection rule that mandates manual unlinking via the PR's Development sidebar panel when a protected issue is GitHub-side linked, and (2) a `!` (MUST) post-merge protected-issue reopen sweep that runs `gh issue view` for each umbrella / staying-OPEN issue and `gh issue reopen` with a #701-citing comment on any auto-close regression. Added two Layer 3 ⊗ anti-patterns to the swarm SKILL Anti-Patterns block. **Secondary encoding (deterministic when invoked):** new `task pr:check-protected-issues` Taskfile target in `tasks/pr.yml` wrapping `scripts/pr_check_protected_issues.py`, which fetches `closingIssuesReferences` for a PR via `gh` and exits non-zero if any protected issue is linked (covered by `tests/cli/test_pr_check_protected_issues.py`). **Tertiary cross-reference:** short entry appended to `meta/lessons.md` (does NOT duplicate the rule body -- per [AXIOM] prose is fallback only; the entry exists for discoverability and explicitly cites #575 (lessons-consumption umbrella) and #633 (pre-PR deterministic-CI umbrella) as the consumption-gap context). Cross-linked `skills/deft-directive-review-cycle/SKILL.md` Post-Merge Verification with the inverse check (protected issues that auto-close MUST be reopened). Cross-references Layer 1 (#167), Layer 2 (#698), workflow umbrella (#642), incident PRs (#700, #401), and the canonical #642 workflow comment https://github.com/deftai/directive/issues/642#issuecomment-4330742436. Closes #701.

### Fixed
- **fix(scripts,tests): `gh release create` uses `--notes-file` instead of inline `--notes` to avoid Windows command-line buffer overflow** (#731, refs #720 e2e harness that surfaced this, refs #721 v0.21.0 cut session anchor, refs #722 PATHEXT helper -- correct, not the bug, refs #74/#716 release pipeline foundation + safety hardening): The deepened `task release:e2e` harness landed by #720 surfaced a real Windows production defect during the v0.21.0 re-cut Phase 3 gate -- the kind of platform-specific issue that mocked unit tests cannot reach by definition (`tests/cli/test_release.py` mocks `subprocess.run`, so the cmd-line length never round-trips through `CreateProcess`). `scripts/release.py::create_github_release` invoked `gh release create v<version> --notes "<promoted CHANGELOG section>"` with the entire release notes inlined as a command-line argument; once the promoted `[<version>]` section grows past the OS command-line buffer (~32 KB on Windows; ARG_MAX 128 KB-2 MB elsewhere) the call fails. `subprocess.run` raises `FileNotFoundError(2, 'The filename or extension is too long', None, 206, None)` because Python wraps Windows error code 206 (`ERROR_FILENAME_EXCED_RANGE`) as `FileNotFoundError` -- and the existing exception handler unconditionally mapped that to the canonical `"gh CLI not found on PATH"` reason, mis-pointing the operator at the #722 PATHEXT shim instead of the cmd-line root cause. The v0.21.0 production cut would have hit the same defect (the promoted `[Unreleased] -> [0.21.0]` section is many KB), landing master in state 2 ("tag pushed, no GitHub release") -- handled by `release_rollback.py::_unwind_tag_pushed_no_release` (#725) but with consumer-visible drift in the meantime. Two coordinated changes in `scripts/release.py::create_github_release`: (1) When `notes` is non-empty, materialise it to a UTF-8 temp file via `tempfile.NamedTemporaryFile(mode="w", encoding="utf-8", newline="", suffix=".md", delete=False)` and pass `--notes-file <path>` to `gh release create` instead of `--notes "<text>"` -- the documented gh CLI mechanism for long-form notes (https://cli.github.com/manual/gh_release_create). The temp file is cleaned up in a `try/finally` regardless of subprocess outcome (success, non-zero exit, FileNotFoundError, any other exception). When `notes` is empty we fall through to `--generate-notes` (gh-side auto-generation from PR titles since the previous tag) so the release body is never blank -- pre-existing behaviour preserved byte-for-byte. (2) Tighten the `FileNotFoundError` handler so `getattr(exc, "winerror", None) == 206` emits a distinct `"gh release create command line exceeded Windows limit (winerror 206, ERROR_FILENAME_EXCED_RANGE) ... see #731"` diagnostic with a hint at the `--notes-file` mitigation. All other `FileNotFoundError` cases (e.g. genuinely missing gh binary) keep the canonical `"gh CLI not found on PATH"` message so existing tests + operator expectations are stable. Out of scope: `release_publish.py`, `release_rollback.py`, `release_e2e.py` use `gh release view/edit/delete` only -- no `--notes` argument carrying large text, so the defect is localised to one function. New `tests/cli/test_release.py::TestCreateGithubReleaseNotesFile731` (8 tests) covers: argv contains `--notes-file <path>` and never `--notes <text>` for non-empty notes; temp file content equals notes verbatim, UTF-8 encoded (em dash round-trip); cleanup on success path; cleanup on non-zero exit; cleanup on FileNotFoundError; winerror=206 emits cmdline-exceeded diagnostic citing #731, NOT canonical gh-not-found; plain FileNotFoundError still maps to canonical `"gh CLI not found on PATH"`; empty notes preserves `--generate-notes` fallback. Self-validation: this is the second iteration in the v0.21.0 cut session of the e2e safety net catching a real defect pre-cut (rollback-as-test in the prior cycle surfaced #722-#725; this cycle surfaced #731 and gave us a clean fix path before any production-touching action). Scope vBRIEF: `vbrief/proposed/2026-04-29-731-release-notes-file-windows-cmdline.vbrief.json`. Closes #731.
- **chore(release): `resolve_version` docstring accuracy + `run_build` env-pop hygiene** (#726 P2 follow-up to #724/#723): Two posterity follow-ups to the `task build` filename / draft-verify fixes (#723, #724). (1) `scripts/resolve_version.py` module docstring no longer claims to be the Taskfile-side resolver -- it has not been since #723 routed `Taskfile.yml` `vars.VERSION` through an inline POSIX `sh:` block (run by go-task's embedded `mvdan/sh` interpreter). The rewritten docstring now states explicitly that the script is an INDEPENDENT Python mirror of the same priority chain (env override > `git describe --tags --abbrev=0` > `0.0.0-dev`), is NOT invoked from `Taskfile.yml`, and exists so Python callers (`scripts/release.py::run_build`, `tests/cli/test_resolve_version.py`, future entry-points) get a single source of truth without silent drift from the canonical Taskfile inline `sh:` block. Test docstring + section header in `tests/cli/test_resolve_version.py` updated to mirror the contract. (2) `scripts/release.py::run_build(project_root, version)` now explicitly `env.pop("DEFT_RELEASE_VERSION", None)` when `version` is falsy. The previous code copied `os.environ` and only set the var when `version` was truthy -- meaning a stale `DEFT_RELEASE_VERSION` leaked from the parent shell (e.g. an interrupted prior `task release` run that exported the var into the operator's session) would silently re-introduce the exact stale-version bug #723 just closed. Contract is now: truthy `version` -> subprocess env carries `DEFT_RELEASE_VERSION=<version>`; falsy / `None` -> subprocess env carries NO `DEFT_RELEASE_VERSION` (Taskfile resolver falls back to git describe). New regression test `TestRunBuildVersionEnv::test_run_build_strips_inherited_env_when_version_none` in `tests/cli/test_release.py` pre-sets `DEFT_RELEASE_VERSION=stale-0.20.0` via `monkeypatch.setenv`, calls `run_build(path, None)`, and asserts the captured subprocess env does NOT contain the key. Refs #726 Greptile P2 review (5/5 "Safe to merge").
- **fix(scripts,skills,tests): release pipeline post-create verify-isDraft within 5s gate** (#724, refs #74 release foundation, refs #716 default-draft contract, refs #721 v0.21.0 cut session anchor, refs #722 gh PATHEXT fix): Closes the ~90-second public-exposure window observed during the v0.21.0 cut where the manual recovery `gh release create v0.21.0 --notes-from-tag --repo deftai/directive` errored on the flag combo BUT had already created the release as public (no `--draft`) before erroring, leaving consumer-visible state diverged from the intended draft state until an operator noticed and ran `gh release edit --draft=true` manually. New `scripts/release.py::verify_release_draft(project_root, version, repo, *, max_attempts=5, interval=1.0, sleep=None)` polls `gh release view v<version> --json isDraft` up to 5 times at 1-second intervals (5s total budget) and routes on three terminal states: (1) `isDraft=true` -> verified safe, no flip; (2) `isDraft=false` -> emits `WARNING: release v<version> landed as public; flipping to draft (defense-in-depth, see #724)` to stderr and immediately invokes `gh release edit v<version> --draft=true`; (3) release-not-found across every poll -> emits a WARN line citing #724 but does NOT fail the pipeline since the create call itself exited 0 (release.yml CI may still be processing). Wired as new pipeline Step 11 (`_TOTAL_STEPS` bumped 10 -> 11) gated on `config.draft and create_succeeded` -- skipped when `--no-draft`, `--skip-release`, or dry-run; defense-in-depth even on the happy path because it catches operator-error variants where an alternate code path sent the release without `--draft`. The new gh subprocess calls reuse the `_resolve_gh()` helper from #722 (Windows PATHEXT shim) and pass `env=os.environ.copy()` so credentials propagate. `skills/deft-directive-release/SKILL.md` Phase 4 documents the gate as an explicit `!` MUST rule with a ⊗ anti-pattern against skipping it (and a sibling rule covering manual recovery paths that bypass `scripts/release.py`); the dry-run preview line count updates from `[N/10]` to `[N/11]`. Tests in `tests/cli/test_release.py`: `TestVerifyReleaseDraft` (6 tests covering happy path / defense flip / timeout / flip-failure / gh-missing / max_attempts=0 short-circuit) plus `TestPipelineVerifyGate` (3 tests covering Step 11 wiring under draft / `--no-draft` / `--skip-release`). Closes #724.
- **fix(scripts,tasks,tests): `task build` reads the actual release version, not a stale Taskfile literal** (#723, refs #74 release foundation, refs #716 safety hardening, refs #721 v0.21.0 cut session anchor): Closes the regression where `task release -- 0.21.0` produced `dist/deft-0.20.0.zip` because `Taskfile.yml` `vars.VERSION` was hard-coded to `0.20.0` and nothing in the release pipeline updated the literal. `Taskfile.yml` replaces the literal `VERSION: 0.20.0` with an inline POSIX `sh:` block (run by go-task's embedded `mvdan/sh` interpreter, so it works cross-platform on Windows / macOS / Linux without requiring `uv`/Python at parse time) that mirrors the same three-tier priority: (1) `$DEFT_RELEASE_VERSION` env var (set by `scripts/release.py::run_build` so the in-flight release version pins the artifact filename); (2) `git describe --tags --abbrev=0` stripped of leading `v` (covers standalone `task build` invocations on a tagged checkout); (3) `0.0.0-dev` fallback for fresh checkouts with no tags or repositories where `git` is unavailable. New `scripts/resolve_version.py` mirrors the same three-tier priority for Python callers and serves as the regression-test surface (the Taskfile inline `sh:` block does NOT invoke this script -- both implementations encode the same canonical priority chain independently). The script writes the resolved version to stdout WITHOUT a trailing newline so go-task's `sh:` capture yields a clean `X.Y.Z` string. `scripts/release.py::run_build(project_root, version)` gains an explicit `version` parameter and propagates `DEFT_RELEASE_VERSION=<version>` via subprocess env when invoking `task build`; `run_pipeline` Step 6 forwards `config.version` so `task release -- 0.21.0` builds `dist/deft-0.21.0.zip`. New `tests/cli/test_resolve_version.py` covers env override / git fallback / dev fallback / git timeout / non-zero exit / empty stdout / bare-`v` tag / main() stdout contract / subprocess smoke (16 tests). New `TestRunBuildVersionEnv` in `tests/cli/test_release.py` covers env-propagation / version=None omission / target-missing skip / Step 6 pipeline wiring (4 tests). Closes #723.
- **fix(scripts): resolve `gh` to its absolute path before subprocess invocation in release scripts** (#721, refs #74 release foundation, refs #716 release safety hardening): On Windows, `gh` is installed as `gh.cmd` (a shell-launcher shim). Python's `subprocess.run(["gh", ...])` does NOT honor `PATHEXT` when resolving `argv[0]` via the OS's `CreateProcess` path, so the launcher cannot be found even when `gh` works fine from the operator's terminal -- which made the four release-pipeline scripts (`scripts/release.py`, `scripts/release_publish.py`, `scripts/release_rollback.py`, `scripts/release_e2e.py`) platform-incomplete on Windows. New shared helper `scripts/release.py::_resolve_gh()` returns `shutil.which("gh")` (which DOES honor `PATHEXT`); every gh subprocess call site in the four scripts now (1) resolves via the helper, (2) passes the absolute path as `argv[0]` (e.g. `C:\Program Files\GitHub CLI\gh.cmd` on Windows), (3) keeps the canonical `gh CLI not found on PATH` reason on `None`, and (4) propagates `env=os.environ.copy()` to `subprocess.run` as defense-in-depth so the child process inherits the operator's PATH and credentials (e.g. `GH_TOKEN` / `GITHUB_TOKEN`). New `tests/cli/test_release_subprocess_path.py` (27 tests) covers the helper delegation contract, the missing-binary fallback for every gh caller across the four scripts, the resolved-path argv[0] behaviour, the `env=` propagation, and the literal Windows `gh.cmd` PATHEXT case. Existing 156 release-script tests continue to pass unchanged. Out of scope for this PR: other gh callers in the repo (`scripts/issue_ingest.py`, `scripts/reconcile_issues.py`, `scripts/pr_check_protected_issues.py`, ...) exhibit the same defect but route to a separate follow-up so the release-pipeline fix lands without blast-radius from refactoring unrelated CLI plumbing. Refs #721 (Closes pending parent agent's rollback validation).

- **fix(tasks): flatten `release:` namespace prefix so documented invocations work end-to-end** (#718, refs #74 foundation, refs #716 safety hardening, refs #233 More Determinism umbrella, refs #642 workflow umbrella, refs #635 epic anchor, refs #709 Repair Authority [AXIOM], refs #710 data-file-conventions follow-up, refs #633 pre-PR deterministic-CI umbrella): PR #712 landed `task release` / `task release:e2e` / `task release:publish` / `task release:rollback` but the wiring (`Taskfile.yml` `includes: release: ./tasks/release.yml` + inner tasks named `release:` / `release:e2e:` / `release:publish:` / `release:rollback:`) caused go-task to concatenate the namespace prefix with each inner task name -- the actual installed names became `release:release`, `release:release:e2e`, `release:release:publish`, `release:release:rollback`, so an operator following `skills/deft-directive-release/SKILL.md` literally hit `Task "release" does not exist` (exit 200) at SKILL Phase 2 immediately. Surfaced by the `release-e2e-validation` sub-agent during Phase 1 pre-flight task-surface check on master @ `41b858e`; demonstrates the value of the SKILL Phase 3 e2e gate landed by #716 (Phase 1 alone caught the defect before any production-touching work happened). Per locked Option 2a in #718: dropped `release: ./tasks/release.yml` from the root `Taskfile.yml`'s `includes:` block, inlined the 4 release task definitions directly under the root `tasks:` block (each as a thin wrapper invoking the corresponding `scripts/release*.py` companion via `uv run python "{{.TASKFILE_DIR}}/scripts/<script>.py" {{.CLI_ARGS}}`), and `git rm tasks/release.yml`. The 4 inline tasks reuse the existing `dir: '{{.USER_WORKING_DIR}}'` consumer-safe CWD pattern (#535) and `env: PYTHONUTF8: "1"` belt-and-suspenders guard (#540); they intentionally declare no `sources:` / `generates:` per `conventions/task-caching.md` (#574) so user-facing recovery flags (`--dry-run` / `--skip-tag` / `--skip-release` / `--allow-dirty` / `--repo` / `--no-draft` / `--allow-low-downloads` / `--allow-data-loss` / `--force-strict-0` / `--owner` / `--keep-repo`) are never silently swallowed by go-task's incremental-build cache. New `tests/content/test_taskfile_release_names.py` (3 tests) is the missing end-to-end guard against regressions: parses `task --list-all` stdout via subprocess and asserts (1) all 4 canonical names appear, (2) no `release:release*` doubled-prefix names appear, and (3) `task release -- --help` dispatches end-to-end (exits 0 + prints argparse usage), proving the full `go-task -> uv run python -> scripts/release.py` chain. Mirrors the skip-on-no-task-binary pattern from `tests/content/test_taskfile_caching.py` (#574). Why this didn't get caught earlier: PR #712's 95+ unit tests in `tests/cli/test_release*.py` exercise `scripts/release*.py` Python entry points directly via `importlib.util.spec_from_file_location`, never invoking through go-task; CI passed for the same reason; pre-merge `task check` runs ruff/mypy/pytest, not the new release task names; Greptile review of #712 didn't catch this -- it's a wiring defect that requires live `task --list-all` to surface. Skill prose in `skills/deft-directive-release/SKILL.md`, the `desc:` strings on the 4 inline tasks, and the CHANGELOG entries from #74/#716 were already correct -- only the wiring was wrong, so this fix touches only the root `Taskfile.yml`, removes `tasks/release.yml`, and adds the guard test (no SKILL or `desc:` churn). Acceptance criteria from #718 satisfied: `task release` dispatches to `scripts/release.py`; `task release:e2e` dispatches to `scripts/release_e2e.py`; `task release:publish` dispatches to `scripts/release_publish.py`; `task release:rollback` dispatches to `scripts/release_rollback.py`; doubled `release:release*` names no longer exist; `task --list-all` shows all 4 canonical names; guard test asserts both presence + absence + dispatch; `task check` passes (2830 baseline + 3 new guard tests). Closes #718.
- **Greptile P1 (PR #401)**: append `--exit-code` to all `madge --circular` invocations in `coding/hygiene.md`, `languages/typescript.md`, and `languages/javascript.md` so cycles fail CI rather than silently passing. (#642, PR #401)
- **Greptile P2 (PR #401)**: add Python `Circular dependencies:` Hygiene subsection in `languages/python.md` referencing `pydeps`/`importlab` and pointing to `coding/hygiene.md` for resolution. (#642, PR #401)
- **Greptile P1 fresh-review fix (PR #401)**: `core/glossary.md` `Rule ownership` definition no longer claims an ownership map lives in `REFERENCES.md` — the map was removed by the trim earlier in this PR (respawned as enforceable structural artifact via PR-A's rule-ownership-map vBRIEF under #635). (#642, PR #401)
- **Greptile P2 fresh-review fix (PR #401)**: `REFERENCES.md` line 102 — secondary `core/glossary.md` entry under "When Planning Multi-Feature Work" updated from "Term definitions" to "Authoritative vocabulary" to match the primary entry. (#642, PR #401)
- **fix(scripts): replace unsafe `git reset --hard HEAD~1` + `git push --force-with-lease` with resolved-SHA forward `git revert` + normal push in `scripts/release_rollback.py`** (#725, refs #716 release safety hardening, refs #722 release._resolve_gh helper, refs #721 rollback-as-test recovery anchor): The state-aware unwind landed in #716 worked correctly through state detection, the time-windowed download-count guard, and `gh release delete --cleanup-tag`, but the commit-unwind + push phase had two coupled defects that blocked end-to-end success on a real protected master branch. (1) `git_reset_head_minus_one` blindly reset to `HEAD~1`, assuming the release-prep commit was the latest commit -- a false assumption the moment ANY commit landed between release-prep and the rollback invocation (e.g. a hot-fix merged after the release commit, then a decision to roll back). The v0.21.0 rollback-as-test demonstrated this concretely: PR #722 merged on top of release-prep `6573335`, and `task release:rollback -- v0.21.0 --allow-data-loss` reset master from `94d1aa5` -> `6573335`, unwinding PR #722 instead of release-prep. (2) `git_force_push_base` ran `git push --force-with-lease origin master`, which GitHub rejected (`GH013: Repository rule violations found ... Cannot force-push to this branch`) -- the default branch protection on `master` disallows force-push from anyone except admins, and even then requires explicit bypass. The script aborted after `gh release delete` already succeeded, leaving master in a half-rolled-back state. Both defects are fixed together because Defect A's fix (forward revert) makes Defect B's force-push moot, and Defect B's branch-protection refusal would have surfaced even with the correct SHA in Defect A's reset path. New helpers in `scripts/release_rollback.py`: (a) `resolve_release_prep_sha(project_root, version)` -- tries `git rev-parse v<version>^{commit}` first (works whenever the local tag still resolves) and falls back to `git log --grep='^chore(release): v<version>' --format=%H -n 1` (walks back from HEAD looking for the canonical release-commit subject defined in `scripts/release.py::_release_commit_subject`). (b) `git_revert_release_commit(project_root, sha)` -- runs `git revert <sha> --no-edit`; on conflict aborts the in-progress revert via `git revert --abort` and returns False with a manual-recovery hint pointing at the new "Manual recovery" section in the module docstring (operator re-runs the revert, resolves conflicts in CHANGELOG.md / ROADMAP.md, runs `git revert --continue`, then `git push origin <base-branch>`). (c) `git_push_base(project_root, base_branch)` -- runs `git push origin <base>` with NO `--force` / `--force-with-lease` (compatible with branch protection). The three unwind branches (`_unwind_local` / `_unwind_tag_pushed_no_release` / `_unwind_released`) now resolve the SHA BEFORE deleting any tag (rev-parse depends on the tag); state 1 (local-only) drops the push entirely (nothing was pushed); states 2 and 3 push the new revert commit forward via `git_push_base`. The deleted helpers `git_reset_head_minus_one` and `git_force_push_base` are no longer present in the active code (a regression test in `tests/cli/test_release_rollback_725.py::TestNoForcePushReferences` strips the docstring and asserts neither `"--force-with-lease"` nor `git_force_push_base(` survives in the active code body). The module docstring's state table is rewritten to reflect the new flow, and a Manual recovery section documents the conflict-refusal path. New tests: `tests/cli/test_release_rollback_725.py` (11 tests) covers resolve_release_prep_sha (rev-parse happy path, grep fallback, both-probes-fail diagnostic, rev-parse-rc0-but-empty-stdout fallthrough), git_revert_release_commit (success path with argv assertion that 'reset' / '--hard' / 'HEAD~1' are absent, conflict + abort + manual-recovery hint, conflict + abort-failure with extra abort diagnostic), git_push_base (argv contains 'push origin <base>' with NO --force flags, failure surfaces stderr, defence-in-depth check on a non-master branch), and the module-level no-force-push invariant. The existing `tests/cli/test_release_rollback.py` (56 tests) is updated to mock the new helpers and assert intervening-commit safety -- with a fake intervening commit, the unwind targets the resolved release-prep SHA (NOT whatever HEAD~1 happens to be). All four release-pipeline scripts continue to use the `release._resolve_gh()` helper from #722. Closes #725.
- **fix(scripts,tasks): deepen `scripts/release_e2e.py::run_rehearsal` from existence-check smoke test to full pipeline mirror against the auto-created temp repo** (#720, refs #716 release safety hardening Q1, refs #722 release._resolve_gh helper, refs #725 forward-revert + normal push in rollback): The rehearsal step landed in #716 was a smoke-test existence check (`gh repo view <temp-repo>` -- enough to prove the provision -> rehearsal -> cleanup loop works without hitting CI) but did NOT actually exercise the release pipeline against the temp repo, despite `skills/deft-directive-release/SKILL.md` Phase 3 prose claiming it does. The CLI surface (`release_e2e.py [--owner] [--dry-run] [--keep-repo] [--project-root]` -- no version / pipeline-orchestration flags) confirmed the gap. Surfaced by the live `release-e2e-validation` sub-agent run on master @ `4a83981`; v0.21.0 was cut despite the gap. Per #716 canonical Q1, the whole point of auto-create + auto-destroy temp repo is exercising the pipeline against a real (throwaway) GitHub remote -- the existence-check approach defeats that. This PR aligns reality with the SKILL prose. New rehearsal flow: (1) clone the local directive repo into a `tempfile.TemporaryDirectory()` via `git clone`; (2) point the clone's origin at the auto-created temp repo via `git remote set-url origin https://github.com/<owner>/<slug>.git`; (3) populate the temp remote with every ref via `git push --mirror`; (4) dispatch `task release -- 0.0.1 --repo <owner>/<slug> --skip-ci --skip-build` from inside the clone (full 10-step pipeline against the temp repo: dirty-tree guard, branch guard, CHANGELOG promotion, ROADMAP refresh, commit, tag, atomic push, gh release create --draft); (5) verify the draft release exists via `gh release view v0.0.1 --json isDraft,tagName,...` (asserts `isDraft=true` and `tagName == v0.0.1`); (6) verify the tag exists on the temp remote via `git ls-remote --tags origin refs/tags/v0.0.1`; (7) dispatch `task release:rollback -- 0.0.1 --repo <owner>/<slug>` to exercise the rollback path against a known-state release (the #725 forward-revert + normal-push flow against a protected default branch). The existing `provision_temp_repo` / `destroy_temp_repo` and the `run_e2e` `try/finally` cleanup pattern stay -- only `run_rehearsal` becomes substantive. Two new flags on `scripts/release.py` (`--skip-ci` / `--skip-build`) keep the rehearsal wall-clock manageable -- both default to False (preserving pre-#720 behaviour) and emit `SKIP (--skip-ci)` / `SKIP (--skip-build)` labels when set; CI / build semantics are covered by the unit-test suite at every commit on master, not by re-running them inside the auto-created temp repo. Each rehearsal step is an isolated mockable function (`clone_repo_to_temp`, `set_origin_to_temp_repo`, `push_mirror`, `dispatch_task_release`, `verify_draft_release`, `verify_tag`, `dispatch_task_release_rollback`) so tests can replace each helper with a mock; CI exercises the orchestration without ever cloning, pushing, or hitting real GitHub. New tests: `tests/cli/test_release_e2e.py` (38 tests) covers each helper individually (argv shape, success / failure paths) plus run_rehearsal orchestration (walks all seven steps in order, short-circuits on first failure, passes the configured version through to the dispatch helper) plus run_e2e (cleanup runs even when rehearsal fails OR raises, --keep-repo skips destroy, --dry-run invokes nothing); `tests/cli/test_release_skip_flags.py` (5 tests) covers the new --skip-ci / --skip-build flags (SKIP label emission, run_ci / run_build NOT invoked, argparse round-trip, defaults preserve pre-#720 behaviour, dataclass defaults). Closes #720.

### Removed
- **Trimmed PR #401 scope to hygiene + AXIOM**: deleted `docs/more-determinism.md` (transformed to vBRIEFs under #635 by PR-A); deleted `core/events.md` (transformed to event-wiring vBRIEFs under #635 by PR-A); removed Rule Ownership Map section and `core/events.md` pointer from `REFERENCES.md` (respawned as enforceable structural artifact via PR-A's rule-ownership-map vBRIEF); removed the `main.md` Decision Making event-pointer addition. Original determinism doc remains reachable via git commit `47034134`; original DDD content via commit `ba253a8`. (#642, PR #401)
